Zhongxiang Xiang embankment, Construction Started to Block the Breach 93

And Build Both Water Diversion and Permeable Dams and Dig an Irrigation Canal. Taking Soil and Transporting Materials are Both Difficult, and it is Difficult to be Optimistic about the Future.

Hankou Correspondence: After the Zhongxiang Xiang River embankment collapsed, the authorities immediately planned to block the breach with all their strength to avoid expanding the flood. On the 7th of this month, Qin Fen, Secretary-General of the Economic Committee, Zheng Zhaojing, County Water Conservancy Department, Yang Yongtai, Chairman of the Provincial Government, Fan Xixu, Committee Member, Liu Shoupeng, Director of the Construction Department, and others, held a meeting in Wuchang and decided that the Provincial Government Economic Committee would jointly form a Remote Embankment Rehabilitation Committee, with Fan Xixu, Xi Dejiong, Shi Yuling, and Chen Ruzhen as members, and Fan was appointed as chairman. An office for the chairman and members was set up, as well as one, two, and three departments. Xi also serves as the head of the first department, managing documents, general affairs, purchasing materials, and handling transportation below Shayang. Shi also serves as the head of the second department, managing labor conscription, worker management, material requisition, and transportation above Shayang. Chen also serves as the head of the third department, managing engineering and materials. On the 9th and 10th, Fan and Qin arrived at Shagang. On the 11th, each department was formally established and began to work on blocking the breach, and another water diversion dam and permeable dam were built and an irrigation canal was excavated. The unfinished project in the fourth section is also continuing to be built. However, the predetermined plan was from the 1st to the 10th of this month for the material purchasing period, and from the 11th to the 30th for the breach blocking period. The entire embankment will be completed by July 15th. Judging from the current situation, it is difficult to proceed so smoothly. There are about several important reasons: ① It is difficult to take soil. The location of the breach in the embankment is far from the Huoshan mountain, which is designated for taking soil, up to 1.5 kilometers, and double the distance back and forth. There is only one line of road in the middle. If you use too many laborers, it will be crowded, and if you use less, it will be difficult to transport more. Now tens of thousands of laborers are taking soil, and they are taking only 1,500-1,600 city squares per day. Sixteen or seventeen people can only take one square of soil. The entire breach needs more than 81,000 squares of soil. If it is calculated as more than ten people per square, more than 1 million laborers are needed. If it is calculated as taking 1,500 squares per day, it will take more than 50 days to take enough. How can the time delay resist the flood season? ② It is difficult to transport materials. The main material is Jingchai, which must be purchased along the Yangtze River and transported from Hankou. Although there is a general transportation station in Hankou, after the Xiang River is diverted by the breach, the river water is extremely dry and it is not easy for ships to travel. Land transportation is even more difficult to reach, and I am afraid that it will not be helpful in time. ③ It is difficult for laborers to live and eat. Tens of thousands of people gather in one place. There is no source of rice. Materials for building sheds, such as bamboo and reed mats, are lacking. Even the location for building sheds, low-lying areas may be flooded, and high-lying areas are too far from the work site, which is also a problem. ④ The health problems of laborers. The weather is hot now, and the laborers work in the hot sun, and they do not know how to pay attention to hygiene. At the moment, a small number of workers, more than 30% of those who are sick. In the future, the number of laborers will increase day by day, and the weather will be hotter, and epidemics will be more difficult to avoid. In addition, the personnel in charge of the material handling department, the first department, and the engineering department, the third department, who are transferred from the former engineering office, have not changed the style of procrastination and procrastination. Moreover, the trust in the laborers has been completely lost, and most of the laborers are not subject to their command, which is also an obstacle. Therefore, it is feared that the completion of the breach closure project within the scheduled 20 days will not be allowed by the facts. (16th)

Reforming the Huai Salt Transport System 95

One Hundred and Twenty Tickets Rotating Directly to Anqing; Twelve Wharf Boatmen and Various Sectors in Datong Strive

Wuhu Correspondence: The Huai salt transported and sold along the Anhui bank has recently undergone changes by salt merchants in accordance with regulations. From the four hundred tickets of Changping Granary salt, one hundred and twenty tickets will be allocated for rotation to Anqing. This has caused panic among the people of Datong, eighty miles upstream of Wuhu. The reason is that Datong's existence as a market town is purely due to its salt wharves. Consequently, there have been numerous appeals to salt merchants to restore the original system. The representatives of the twelve wharf salt boats in Yangzhou, who made a large-scale petition, have taken concerted action. The outcome of this evolving situation depends on whether the salt merchants can retract their original proposal. The opposition from the commercial and industrial sectors in Datong and the process of reforming the rotational transport are summarized from the news gathered over the past few days and recorded as follows:

As a transshipment hub, it has become a commercial town due to salt and has progressed into one of the commercial ports along the Yangtze River in Anhui Province. In 1933, Miao Qiujie, the Salt Transport Commissioner of Lianghuai, reformed the salt system and set up a warehouse in Anqing to pilot the rotational transport system, designating the surrounding seven counties as the trial sales area. The commercial and industrial sectors in Datong believed that the seizure of the salt market was tantamount to cutting off their livelihood. After numerous appeals, several thousand laborers risked their lives to stage a petition across the river. The Ministry of Finance ordered the Anhui Bank Salt Transport Bureau to handle the matter and dispatched section chief Yu Quji and others to work with the Datong military and police organs to find a solution. The only condition was to maintain the Datong salt market, and the Huai salt would no longer be directly transported to Anqing. This resolved the initial crisis. In the past two or three years, although there has been the intention to establish a Central Salt Warehouse, Anhui Bank still considers Datong as the main hub. Unexpectedly, recently, Yangzhou salt merchants, in order to reduce transportation costs, have again proposed to use rotational transport, directly transporting the salt to Anqing for sale. Although various sectors in Datong have sent numerous letters and telegrams requesting the Anhui Bank Salt Transport Bureau and the salt merchants to restore the old system, there has been no effect. Therefore, feeling the immediate impact on their interests, the representatives of the twelve wharf salt boats first went to the residences of the salt merchants in Yangzhou to petition. The laborers in Datong then continued to appeal, and the situation escalated. It has now reached a point of no return. Looking at their warning letter to the Yangzhou Four Banks Guild and Huainan merchant Jia Songping and others, it states, "If you stubbornly refuse to see the light and willingly become the troublemakers, the laborers, in order to uphold the Ministry's orders and proposals (referring to the events of 1933) and maintain their own lives, are prepared for a sea of blood in the waters of the Yangtze River. Even if your momentum is strong, we fear it will be difficult to reach Anqing. You have money, but the laborers have their lives. We are willing to sacrifice everything." This shows their intense attitude. Furthermore, a letter from the General Guild of the eighteen gangs of twelve wharf salt transport Jiang boats states, "It has been found that transporting Huai salt to Anqing harms the livelihoods of all the workers in your gang and affects the commerce of Datong. We have already petitioned the Ministry of Finance and the Anhui Bank Salt Transport Bureau, which have repeatedly issued strict orders to stop it. Now, based on previous reasons, Jia (Songping) and Zhong (Weiyu) and others intentionally overthrow the Ministry's orders, destroy the proposals, despise the workers, and willingly become troublemakers. The unemployed workers and your gang are in the same boat, and we should work together." This further shows that the workers and boatmen in Datong and the twelve wharfs, whose livelihoods depend on salt, are indeed taking concerted action. (June 17)

Two Lives Crushed by Shanghai-Huning Railway Car

Wuxi 99

Exempting Pig Trade Business Tax

The Lihengxing, Hengyifeng, Hengsheng, Ruichang, Hengda, and other pig trade businesses in Beidang have recently been assessed for pig trade business tax by the Business Tax Collection Bureau, and have been forced to pay back taxes. They specifically submitted requests to the Ministry of Finance and the Department of Finance to exempt them from payment. The Department of Finance issued a reply, stating that the business tax collected by the brokers is collected from the sellers who invest in the trade, and that those who are both brokers and operate sales with their own capital should pay business tax for sales operations. These are two separate matters, and the sections presented are clearly misunderstandings. After receiving the reply, each pig trade business stated that this tax had never been collected before, so they had not collected it from the sellers who invested in the trade over the years. Furthermore, each business does not use its own capital and only sells on behalf of customers. Before the new tax is established, it is unfair to collect old taxes first. Yesterday, they jointly submitted a request to the county government, asking it to instruct the tax bureau to approve the exemption from payment.

Local News

China Flying Club Flying Training Class 103

Opening Ceremony Held Yesterday

President and Vice President Deliver Training Speeches

Training Begins on the 22nd

The opening ceremony of the first flying training class of the China Flying Club was held at 10:00 AM yesterday at the Longhua Flying Port. Thirty-four students and dozens of guests, including Dai Enji, attended. President Wu Tiecheng led the ceremony and delivered a speech. After the ceremony, a photo was taken, and a flying performance was held. It is reported that the flying class is scheduled to begin training on the 22nd. The details of the ceremony are recorded as follows:

Venue Arrangement

The China Flying Club established a flying class to train primary aviation personnel. A total of forty people were accepted, and thirty-four people paid their fees and enrolled. The registration procedures have been completed. The opening ceremony was held as scheduled yesterday at Longhua Port. A colorful arch was erected at the entrance, guarded by police officers. The venue was surrounded by ropes, leading to the airfield. Two of the club's latest trainer aircraft were parked there. The venue was set up inside the hangar of the China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC). The flags of the Kuomintang and the Republic of China, the portrait of Sun Yat-sen, the club's flag emblem, and photos of the aircraft naming ceremony were hung in the middle. On both sides, the CNAC's mail planes and engines were displayed, with explanations in Chinese and English for the students and guests to visit. The arrangement was extremely simple and elegant.

Attendees

Thirty-four students, all dressed in yellow cloth flying suits, arrived at the venue at around 9:00 AM. They were all very energetic and lively. The attendees also included club committee members Wang Xiaolai, Yao Xijiu, Li Dachao, Zeng Yijing, Li Ruyan, Wu Yunzhu, Dai Enji, Zhou Xuexiang of the General Labor Union, Lin, the director of the Postal Bureau, Cai Jinjun, the director of the Public Security Bureau, and female aviator Li Xiaqing, who recently returned from studying in Europe. President Wu Tiecheng arrived in Shanghai from Beijing yesterday morning and arrived at the venue at around 9:30 AM. The students lined up in front of the aircraft for roll call. President Wu personally inspected them. Then, the Save the Nation aircraft, piloted by instructor Yang Guozhu, flew to the venue. The ceremony then began.

President's Speech

President Wu Tiecheng presided over the opening ceremony, led the attendees in paying respects, and delivered a training speech, saying: "Distinguished guests, students, the opening of the China Flying Club's training class today marks the beginning of the first page in the history of civil aviation in our country. Sun Yat-sen's last words stated that the fundamental methods for building a prosperous and strong country are to make full use of talent, land, resources, and smooth flow of goods. Our country is vast, rich in resources, and has a large population, but it cannot achieve prosperity and strength because resources cannot be fully utilized and goods cannot flow smoothly. The biggest reason for this is the lack of complete transportation, which prevents the country from being truly unified, the nation from being truly united, and resources from being fully developed. For example, Guangdong Province does not produce rice, and its food supply comes from Vietnam and Siam, with an annual outflow of 70 million yuan. The neighboring province of Hunan produces abundant rice, but due to transportation difficulties, it accumulates inland and cannot be transported out to meet the needs of other provinces. The same is true for Shanghai. The lack of supply and demand is caused by the separation of transportation and cannot be mediated. This is the most important economic problem in our country that needs to be solved urgently. The government has been working hard on construction in recent years, and its main task is to build the transportation industry. Its decisions, such as economic defense, are also in progress. In recent years, the gradual completion of the national highway network, the construction of inland railways, and the opening of air routes have all achieved good results. Convenient transportation shortens leisure time and lengthens time, allowing Chinese people to travel around the country as if they were in one room. We should pay more attention to valuable time. In one's life, the time of youth is only twenty or thirty years. How should we make full use of it to develop human abilities, benefit society and the country, and work hard for personal career? The China Aviation Association is a public group that assists the government in building aviation. The Flying Club is also a public organization, and it is still an innovation in the country. Its purpose is to cultivate civil aviation talents to develop civil aviation and reserve pilots for the country to act as reserves for the air force. All of you students have come from afar to enroll and receive training, and you should also share this aspiration. I hope you will keep in mind the purpose of serving the country. The Eurasian and China National Aviation Corporation here has factories and machines for you to study, which is a rare opportunity. I hope you will study hard. The hope of our country in the future lies in the enlightened, intelligent, and capable youth. I hope all of you will strive to do your best."

Wang Xiaolai's Speech

Vice President Wang Xiaolai then delivered a speech, saying, "We are carrying out the spirit of Sun Yat-sen's last words and realizing the cause of aviation to save the country. Therefore, the China Flying Club was established and the flying class was opened. This is not only to assist the government in building air defense, but also to develop civil aviation. Its significance has been explained in detail by President Wu. The flying class is now the first class and has the nature of a pilot and model. Its performance will have a great impact on later generations. I hope all of you students will be tireless and study hard to achieve the goal of being a model for the country and later generations. I have been engaged in the aviation industry and have the ambition to have my ten children study aviation. Due to their age, they have not been able to enroll yet, but I will definitely achieve this goal in the future. Flying training, although it is just starting in our country, has already been advocated in books, such as 'If you don't fly, you're done, but if you fly, you'll soar into the sky' and 'A meteoric rise,' which all encourage flying. There are also two flying generals in history, such as Zhang Fei of the Three Kingdoms and Yue Fei, who were loyal to the Han Dynasty and wholeheartedly served the country. The greatness of their spirit is enough to be a model for all of you. I hope that after you graduate, you will work hard for the country." After the speech, music was played and the ceremony concluded. A group photo was taken at the venue to commemorate the occasion. Instructors Chen Zhiguang, Chen Shenhu, and Yang Guozhu then piloted three aircraft, carrying the guests on a circular flight around the venue. The event ended at around 12:00 noon.

Preparing for the Class

The training class is scheduled to begin training at Longhua Port at dawn on the 22nd. It will be divided into two classes, morning and afternoon, with instructors Chen Buzhou, Yang Guozhu, Chen Zhiguang, Chen Shenhu, and others serving as flying instructors. The academic subjects will be taught by Li Ruyan, Chen Buzhou, and others. The classrooms will be set up in the club on Albert Road. It is reported that some students have come to Shanghai from Hanzhong, Tianjin, Qingdao, and other places specifically to enroll. They have all moved into the club to stay. After the club was expanded, several dormitories have been opened, but the students are responsible for their own meals. The club attaches great importance to the discipline of the students. Therefore, there are fixed times for getting up, resting, and attending classes. They get up at 5:30 AM every morning and gather at the airfield at 6:00 AM. Lights must be turned off at 10:00 PM in the evening. As for extracurricular activities, they have been guided to organize a sports club to build their physique and a reception room has been set up for proper social interactions. The reading room is equipped with various daily newspapers and various musical instruments for entertainment. It is also learned that Ms. Chen Suren wants to join the first training class and has asked the club to accommodate her. The club has approved her request and will allow her to complete the procedures for training after she passes the physical examination. The registration for the second class of students will begin soon.

Chamber of Commerce Smuggling Problem Research Conference Drafts Proposal Yesterday 105

Sixteen trade associations in the city, including the silk and satin industry and the chemical raw materials industry, held a joint meeting some days ago to discuss the rejection of smuggled goods. It was decided to first select Luo Qinghua and eleven others to form a smuggling problem research conference. On the one hand, the committee will draft a plan and ask the members' congress of the chamber of commerce to select representatives from various industries to organize the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Smuggling Inspection Committee to lead various industries to assist the government in investigating and suppressing smuggled goods. The committee held a meeting at 4:00 PM yesterday, and more than ten committee members attended. It was decided that the various industries should provide rules on smuggling inspection for research. A proposal to the congress was drafted, which reads as follows: "Regarding the proposal, since the occurrence of smuggling in North China, the import of smuggled goods that evade taxes has been increasing day by day. The impact of this is not only the destruction of the national tax system and the loss of tax revenue, but also the fact that our dying industry and commerce will suffer a major blow and will not be able to survive. The government authorities have clearly stipulated laws and strictly investigated and suppressed smuggling in order to prevent smuggling and protect legitimate commerce. They have also stipulated the collection and registration of transit cargo sales certificates and the issuance of registered cargo sales certificates. The Chamber of Commerce and trade associations are responsible for handling the matter. The government is determined to thoroughly prevent smuggling and improve the organization of trade associations. Our Chamber of Commerce and trade associations are all legitimate business groups. We should respond to this major event that affects our own interests and exercise the powers granted to us by the government to defend ourselves. We should also ensure that legitimate commercial goods are not affected by this. Shanghai is a transportation hub for the north and south, and the commercial situation is complex. Today, smuggling is rampant, and cunning people are deceiving in every way. Precautions should be even stricter. It is difficult to achieve thorough rejection of smuggling unless each trade association improves its own organization, advises its members to reject smuggled goods, strictly implements inspections, and acts with conscience to supervise each other. In order to consolidate the front line and maintain a unified pace in the handling of smuggling affairs among the various industries, so as to fully exert the power of rejection of smuggling, it is necessary for the Chamber of Commerce to organize a special committee led by three business leaders to exercise the responsibility of supervision and guidance. With this organization, we can maintain connections between the upper and lower levels and among the various industries. Even if there are obstacles, they can be easily resolved. This is a necessary measure to strictly implement smuggling suppression. Therefore, our association and others have held a joint meeting and decided that the congress should pass the resolution and hand it over to the executive committee to select representatives from various industries to organize the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Smuggling Inspection Committee, formulate regulations, lead the various trade associations, assist the government in investigating and suppressing smuggled goods, so as to maintain the national treasury and ensure the safety of industry and commerce. We have recorded the proposal and respectfully await your decision. Proponents: Luo Qinghua, Xu Limin, Lou Fengzhao of the Silk and Satin Association; Xie Zhongfu of the Chemical Raw Materials Association; Ke Ganchen of the Cotton Cloth Association; Shen Tianxin of the Knitting Association; Zheng Zenan of the Sugar Association; Ge Weian of the Seafood and Grocery Association; Jin Runxiang of the Paper Association; Ma Jisheng of the Cosmetics Association; Cai Shengbai of the Electrical Silk Weaving Factory; Ba Lingyun of the Chinese and Foreign Grocery Association; Liu Zhiyuan of the Salt Association; Chen Zixiang of the North-South Goods Exchange Association; Le Fucheng of the Candy, Biscuit, and Canned Food Association; Ling Zhijia and Zhu Binglu of the Ginseng and Bird's Nest Association; Zhao Xianji of the Hardware Association; and Xi Runeng of the Western Dye Association."

Public Concession Factory Inspection Agreement 109

A Factory Inspection Bureau will be established with an equal number of Chinese and foreign staff

Inspectors will be selected for a three-year term

The Ta Lu Pao reports that the Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC) will study the draft agreement regarding factory inspection in the Public Concession, negotiated between the SMC and the Chinese authorities, at its meeting next Wednesday. Negotiations on this matter have been ongoing for over five years, and the SMC is only now considering it for the first time. The document was delivered to Fessenden, the Secretary-General of the Shanghai Municipal Government, by Yu Hongjun yesterday. According to Fessenden's statement to the Ta Lu Pao reporter, he believes the SMC will approve the final draft of the agreement. He and Secretary-General Yu have exchanged opinions repeatedly, believing that the agreement is the only possible route to a compromise satisfactory to both parties. Although the entire contents of the agreement are not yet known, it is rumored that the SMC will not be granted the right to implement Chinese factory laws in factories owned by foreigners enjoying extraterritoriality. The principle agreed upon by both parties is to advise foreign-owned factories. If this approach is ineffective, the SMC will use its licensing authority to crack down on factories that deliberately violate the provisions of the factory inspection agreement. However, even with the agreement in place, the SMC does not intend to implement all of Chinese factory laws, only the part concerning factory inspection. This will be the first phase of the national government's broad program to improve industrial conditions across the country. According to current plans, the agreement will take effect at the beginning of next month. Since the industrial section of the SMC already has a basic framework for factory inspection, the implementation of the new agreement is not expected to require a long period of preparation. A factory inspection bureau will soon be established in the Public Concession, with an equal number of Chinese and foreign staff. These inspectors must be familiar with the structure of Chinese factory laws and will initially be on probation for six months. They must also possess knowledge of industrial chemistry, construction, mechanical science, and engineering. The agreement will be valid for three years, after which each party may decide to extend it, amend it, or completely abolish it. The current agreement will serve as a basis for future discussions with the French Concession authorities on a similar agreement.

Solar Eclipse This Afternoon, Faint Eclipse Visible in the City 112

According to the Central News Agency, there will be a solar eclipse today. If the weather is clear and cloudless, a faint eclipse will be visible here between 1:04 PM and 3:20 PM. The next solar eclipse will not be visible again for five years, i.e., September 17, 1941.

According to a French translation from the Shanghai Daily, the Xu Jiahui Observatory reports that June 19th is the date of the solar eclipse. The situation at that time will be as follows: the shadow of the moon will not exceed 140 kilometers in width. This shadow will first appear in the Mediterranean, then pass through Greece, the Black Sea, and reach the Caucasus, before moving on to Soviet Russia and northern Manchuria, and disappearing at 180 degrees longitude in the Pacific Ocean. The start of the solar eclipse will be at 10:45 AM, counting for places like Soviet Russia's Qian Sike and Boli, as well as Japan's Xiaoching and Murane. The duration of the total eclipse will be between one minute and one minute and thirty-two seconds, and the area where the total eclipse is visible will be in Bayika. Only a part of the solar eclipse will be visible, and only one-third of the sun will be obscured by the shadow of the moon. From this perspective, the people of Shanghai will pass through the solar eclipse unknowingly. As for the precise time when the solar eclipse is visible in Shanghai, the eclipse will begin at 1:04 PM and end at 3:20 PM.

Temporary Cholera Prevention Office Requests Cooperation from the Medical Community 113

The Shanghai Temporary Cholera Prevention Office requests continued cooperation from the medical community for cholera prevention and treatment

The chairman and members of the Shanghai Temporary Cholera Prevention Office deeply appreciate the efforts of medical colleagues in Shanghai in assisting with cholera prevention and control in the past few years. Cholera is a summer disease in our country. In Shanghai, although it sometimes appears as early as April or as late as October, it mostly occurs in July, August, and September, and is a cyclical epidemic, occurring about once every two or three years. For example, in Shanghai in 1929, there were 3,555 cases; in 1932, there were 4,296 cases; in 1930, there were only 127 cases; in 1931, there were 482 cases; and in 1934 and 1935, it was almost non-existent. Due to the efforts of all parties, the mortality rate of cholera in Shanghai has greatly decreased, from 30-50% to 7%. In terms of the total number, the mortality rate of poor patients who quickly seek medical attention in public hospitals seems to be lower than that of those who delay. Whether cholera will recur this summer is uncertain, but the central and municipal health authorities have made adequate preparations. In this matter, the assistance of opening clinic doctors and other sectors is extremely necessary. Through the years of efforts by the central and municipal health authorities, such as implementing cholera prevention, holding public lectures, distributing manuals and leaflets, posting slogans and illustrations, and contacting hospitals to admit patients, the public has gained a deep understanding of cholera. Furthermore, because patients are admitted to free hospitals early and receive the good results of intravenous saline infusions, even the ignorant and uninformed are happy to seek medical attention. All isolation hospitals and plague hospitals in the city have a total of over 1,000 beds, providing free accommodation for cholera patients, but this may not be widely known. During the summer, private practice doctors commonly see gastrointestinal inflammations similar to cholera, some of which may be atypical cholera. Therefore, to assist health authorities, please pay attention to the following items:

Free stool tests: All suspected cholera stools must be tested using appropriate methods. If private individuals do not have this equipment, they can send them to the Municipal Testing Institute for free diagnosis.

Sending to plague hospitals: Suspected or confirmed cholera patients should be immediately sent to the hospital for treatment. Cholera patients must be hospitalized for treatment for two reasons: (A) to prevent the spread of infection, and (B) hospitals are well-equipped and can provide comprehensive care and appropriate treatment.

Provide prevention methods: Try to make patients understand the importance of the following: (A) Carefully preserve food, fruits, and other items to avoid contamination by dirty utensils and flies; (B) Use tap water for drinking, cooking, and washing; (C) Receive cholera vaccination in the summer. Health authorities in various cities in Shanghai conduct universal vaccination every summer, and many have benefited. When vaccinating people, private practice doctors are asked to use vaccines made from local cholera bacteria. These vaccines can be purchased from local health laboratories or the Nanjing Central Epidemic Prevention Office at a very low cost. Shanghai Temporary Cholera Prevention Office, June 15, 1936.

You can send stools to the following laboratories for free testing:

Name Address Telephone

Public Concession Pathology Laboratory 223 Hankou Road 22410, 2419

French Concession Health Bureau Laboratory 207 Jin Shenfu Road 74574

Shanghai Municipal Health Laboratory 198 Qiujiang Road 46398

After the government invited bids and established the Party and National Flag Production and Sales Bureau, it was entrusted with exclusive authority to improve manufacturing and unify distribution. Jianghai Customs Proclamation: Receiving or Purchasing Goods Evading Customs Duties Will Be Subject to Criminal Penalties 116

Subject to the crime of receiving stolen goods under Article 349 of the Criminal Code

Jianghai Customs has issued a proclamation stating that receiving or purchasing goods that have evaded customs duties will be subject to criminal penalties under the crime of receiving stolen goods. The proclamation states: In accordance with the order of the Ministry of Finance, anyone who receives or purchases goods that have evaded customs duties shall be subject to criminal penalties in accordance with Article 349 of the Criminal Code. This shall be followed and a transcript of Article 349 of the Criminal Code is recorded on the left. Article 340 of the Criminal Code, anyone who receives stolen goods shall be sentenced to imprisonment for no more than three years, detention, or a fine of no more than 500 yuan. Those who transport, store, purchase, or act as guarantors for stolen goods shall be sentenced to imprisonment for no more than five years, detention, or a fine of no more than 1,000 yuan, or both. Property obtained from stolen goods shall be regarded as stolen goods. All merchants, etc., are hereby informed. This proclamation is hereby issued.

Chamber of Commerce Writes to the Shanghai Municipal Council Opposing the Reduction of Rickshaws 124

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce wrote to the Public Concession Shanghai Municipal Council yesterday, stating that the gradual reduction of rickshaws in the concession, with transportation tools completely replaced by cars and trams, is a proposal that, apart from directly and indirectly benefiting the companies themselves, only a very small number of citizens with superior living conditions may agree with. It completely disregards the livelihood of the tens of thousands of laborers within the concession. The position of your council is different, as it is entrusted by more than one million Chinese and foreign citizens within the concession to handle public affairs. All municipal facilities should not only seek convenience for a small number of people but should be designed with the greatest number of citizens in mind. Especially, the livelihood of the laborers should not be ignored. If the proposal to gradually reduce rickshaws within the concession is implemented, it may win the praise of a few in terms of urban appearance, but the increase in the number of unemployed people will be a cause for concern in terms of public security. A wise politician should not only pursue superficial grandeur but should also pay attention to such practical issues. Therefore, we are writing to request that your council give serious consideration to the proposal to reduce rickshaws and not approve it lightly. This is what we earnestly hope for.

Meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees of the Lawyers Association 126

Municipal Party Department's Political Prisoner Rehabilitation Committee 128

Second Meeting Held Yesterday

The Municipal Party Department, in order to reform political prisoners and correct their thinking, established the Political Prisoner Rehabilitation Committee. The second meeting was held yesterday (the 18th) at 10 AM in the department's conference room. Details of the meeting are as follows:

Committee Members Present: Committee members present included Tong Xingbai, Lu Jingshi, Jiang Huaishu, Wang Longzhang, Xing Wan, Jiang Hao, Huang Xianggu, Wu Xianren, Zhu Jiarang, Zhang Jianming, Xu Hongzao, He Chengfu, Zhang Yingzeng, Zhang Xiaotong, and over ten others. Tong Xingbai presided, Shen Chunhui recorded, and after formalities, the chairman presented a report.

Reported Matters: (1) The investigation into the educational backgrounds of political prisoners in Jiangsu Second Prison has been completed. There are 97 political prisoners, broken down as follows: 4 with university degrees, 17 with secondary school degrees (including 2 women), 7 with primary school degrees (including 2 women), 2 civil servants, 15 small business owners, 4 farmers, 39 workers, and 9 unemployed (including 2 women). (2) After the recent transfer of 6 political prisoners from the French Concession Special Zone Prison to the Penitentiary, only 3 men and 1 woman remain. However, new prisoners are expected soon. (3) The British Concession Special Zone Sub-Prison currently has 2 female prisoners, but 2 more female prisoners are expected soon. In total, there are 103 political prisoners (including 9 female prisoners). After the report, the first phase implementation plan for rehabilitation was discussed and decided.

Rehabilitation Plan: "First Phase Implementation Plan for Rehabilitation" (1) "Rehabilitation Period": Three months per phase, twice a week, one hour each time. (2) "Rehabilitation Location": Based on the location of the prisons, divided into three locations, each further divided into groups based on the number of prisoners and their educational level. (3) "Rehabilitation Method": Divided into two types: (A) Group training, (B) Individual counseling. The two will be used alternately. An examination will be held at the end of each phase. (4) "Rehabilitation Materials": A separate political training outline will be compiled and distributed to each rehabilitator for use in group training and individual counseling. The rehabilitators will decide on the content of the training based on the ideological responses of the prisoners after the talks. (5) "Rehabilitators": Each group will have a designated rehabilitator responsible for all rehabilitation matters for that group. Each rehabilitator must report to the committee once a week on their progress.

Group Rehabilitation: Group assignments: 4 university degree holders in one group, 17 secondary school degree holders (including 2 women) in two groups, 7 primary school degree holders (including 2 women) in one group, 2 civil servants in one group, 15 small business owners in two groups, 4 farmers in one group, 39 workers in four groups, 9 unemployed (including 2 women) in one group. The Jiangsu Second Prison, 3 men from the French Concession Special Zone Prison in one group, 1 woman in one group, 2 women from the British Concession Sub-Prison in one group.

Yungli Chemical Industries Issues Corporate Bonds to Repay Loans 130

Reception for Banking Industry on the 22nd

Yungli Chemical Industries Co., Ltd., for the construction of the Daodu Ammonium Sulfate Plant, borrowed 5.5 million yuan in national currency from five banks, including the Bank of China, Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, Kincheng Banking Corporation, China & South Sea Bank, and Chekiang Industrial Bank, in the spring of 1934. After signing the contract, the payment was made on November 1st of the same year, with an annual interest rate of 7% and a term of three years. The above five banks formed the Yungli Company Loan Syndicate. Now, the company has negotiated with the syndicate and obtained approval from the Executive Yuan to issue corporate bonds of 5.5 million yuan, issued on May 1st, with an interest rate of 7% and a term of nine years, to be fully repaid by April 30, 1945. Only interest will be paid for the first three years, and principal will be repaid starting from the fourth year. The corporate bonds will be used to repay the banks from which the loans were obtained. The allocation method will also be based on the proportion of the original loans. The company's entire assets will serve as collateral. To celebrate the imminent completion of the Capital Ammonium Sulfate Plant, the company will host a visit for the investing banks. The Bank of China, Central Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, Chekiang Industrial Bank, Continental Bank, Kincheng Banking Corporation, China & South Sea Bank, Yien Yieh Commercial Bank, and China Development Finance Corporation are scheduled to travel from Shanghai to Nanjing on the 20th, visit on the 21st, and return to Shanghai on the 22nd. Banks in the Capital were already hosted last Sunday.

The marriage was initially harmonious, but soon the defendant's behavior changed, and he frequently engaged in extramarital affairs, contracting gonorrhea, which has persisted for several years. Because it is an incurable disease, the plaintiff believes it indirectly affects childbearing. Thus, after seven years of marriage, they have not had children, and there is no joy to be found in family or life. Furthermore, the defendant is violent by nature and often resorts to physical abuse when displeased. He also disregards the family finances, forcing the plaintiff to borrow from her family to make ends meet. The suffering she has endured over the years is beyond description. Continuing in this manner will sever her lifelong happiness. Therefore, she is forced to request a divorce. Yesterday morning, Magistrate Sun held a court session. Lin Shenshi did not appear and was represented by her lawyer, Pan Renxi, who reiterated the plaintiff's claims. The defendant, Lin Xingyuan, denied any abuse, claimed that he gave all his earnings to his wife, denied having gonorrhea, and opposed the divorce. The magistrate ordered the court clerk to take Lin to the forensic doctor for an examination to determine if he had any disease. Upon resuming the session, the magistrate told Lin Xingyuan that the medical examiner had diagnosed him with gonorrhea. Lin replied that he had chronic gonorrhea, but it could be cured. He requested that the court order them to remain together. At this point, the magistrate ordered the commencement of arguments. After the lawyers for both sides presented their cases, the magistrate declared the debate closed and set a date for pronouncement of the judgment.

Sixteen-Year-Old Coppersmith Apprentice Zhu Jingfang Commits Suicide by Leaving a Suicide Note 134

Not a Sudden Illness, but Swallowing Opium, Letter States Revenge for Parents

Zhu Jingfang, a sixteen-year-old apprentice coppersmith from Nanjing working at the Gongping Copper and Iron Factory on Shilu Road in the South City, committed suicide. At 8:20 PM the other night, after night watch duty at the factory, he went upstairs to bed. Around midnight, Wang Chunfang, a clerk in the factory's rice room, heard Jingfang suddenly vomiting and moaning. Suspecting a sudden illness, but seeing his face pale, he immediately informed the owner, Zhu Shouju, who hired a car to take him to Shanghai Hospital. It was discovered that he had swallowed opium to commit suicide. Due to the severity of the poisoning, medical treatment was ineffective, and he died shortly thereafter. The medical center was notified, and it was found that the deceased had left four pairs of suicide notes addressed to the Futai Pawnshop on Yanjia Lane in Suzhou, to be delivered to his older brother, Zhu Yifang. Enclosed were letters to his older sister and younger brother, which read, in part, "To my dear brother Yifang, now we are forever separated. My death is inevitable. Of the four of us, I rely entirely on you to fight for our parents' revenge. Please do not grieve." The local court sent a prosecutor and medical examiner to the scene at 11 AM yesterday to conduct an inspection. It was confirmed that the death was caused by poisoning before death. In addition to filling out a coroner's report for the record, the factory was ordered to prepare a coffin and arrange the funeral, pending the family's retrieval of the body for burial.

Song Ziang, Just Granted Probation for Embezzlement, Commits Fraud and Breach of Trust 138

Li Yufu, Manager of Yitai Exchange, Sues

A Total of 13,000 Yuan Paid to the Defendant

Defendant Absent from Court Yesterday

Song Ziang, a key employee in the accounting department of the China General Omnibus Company, recently embezzled over ten thousand copper coins from the company, which he was unable to repay. He surrendered himself to the police and was handed over to the First Special District Court, which sentenced him to seven months imprisonment, suspended for two years. Now, Li Yufu, the manager of the Yitai Exchange on Broadway, through his lawyer, Lu Qi, has filed a lawsuit in the District Court accusing Song Ziang of fraud and breach of trust. The lawsuit states that the defendant, as an agent in the accounting department of the China General Omnibus Company, invited the plaintiff, Yitai Exchange, to enter into a contract to sell copper coins on December 12, 1931, depositing a guarantee deposit. The contract stipulated that the plaintiff would sell all the copper coins from the company's ticket sales every day, for a term of one year, with the provision that the contract would continue in effect after the expiration date until June 30 of this year. Initially, both parties complied with the contract, delivering the copper coins and paying the money on the same day. For several years, the relationship was harmonious. However, recently the defendant, using the pretext that the company was facing economic difficulties and the market was sluggish, expressed concern that it would be difficult to collect money after the copper coins were issued, and that there would be negligence. Therefore, if the plaintiff wished to purchase a certain amount of copper coins, they would have to pay the price in advance. For the sake of business, the plaintiff had no choice but to comply. Therefore, whenever the plaintiff decided to purchase coins, they had to pay the company's accounting department in advance and receive a stamped receipt, waiting for the company to send the copper coins on the same day or a few days later. The plaintiff had become accustomed to this and had no doubts. Unexpectedly, on the 4th of this month, the plaintiff paid the company's accounting department 3,000 yuan in legal tender with the Exchange's 12th issue No. 2839, and received a receipt. The defendant then fraudulently told the plaintiff's representative that the Central Mint was urgently requesting the delivery of copper coins due to the conversion of subsidiary coins, and that if the Exchange did not pay in advance, there would be insufficient supply in the future and it would be difficult to purchase coins. The defendant strongly urged the plaintiff to pay more in advance to secure the purchase, so as to avoid being unable to purchase coins in the future. On the 5th, the defendant took another 5,000 yuan from the plaintiff's immediate demand draft from the Bank of Communications and a ten-day bill of exchange from the plaintiff's letter of credit Exchange in the name of the company for 5,000 yuan, totaling 13,000 yuan in legal tender. Apart from receiving copper coins worth 5,000 yuan, the defendant consistently delayed sending the copper coins despite repeated requests. On the 8th, the defendant suddenly disappeared. The plaintiff, unable to do anything else, published a notice declaring the draft and bill of exchange invalid, and reported the matter to the Sixth District Public Security Bureau and the Nanjing Road Police Station. The newspaper reported that the defendant had secretly sold over ten thousand copper coins from the company and surrendered himself to the police headquarters. The plaintiff then understood the full story. The defendant, using the name of the company's accounting department, took a large amount of drafts and bills of exchange from the plaintiff and Xuan Da Exchange, converting them into his own assets and transferring them to cover other debts, causing the plaintiff to be deceived and suffer a loss of 8,000 yuan. This is not permissible under the law and principles of justice. Furthermore, the plaintiff's payment was not made to the defendant personally, but to the company's accounting department, as evidenced by the company's receipt. It was the defendant's duty to use this money to purchase and send the copper coins, but instead, he illegally converted it into his own assets and transferred it to cover his personal debts, causing the plaintiff to have the already declared invalid drafts and bills of exchange presented by others, resulting in a loss of credit and potential litigation over the realization of the drafts. Therefore, the plaintiff requests legal action and seeks the return of the drafts and bills of exchange. Yesterday, Magistrate Zhao Yongzhou held a court session. Neither party was present. After the plaintiff's lawyer, Lu, made his statement, the defendant's lawyer, Yu Xiangqin, appeared in court and stated that the case was purely a commercial transaction, amounting at most to a civil debt dispute. The defendant was unable to attend court because of matters in Suzhou and requested a postponement, promising to attend the hearing. The magistrate ordered the court to postpone the hearing.

Impelled by Poverty, Elderly Man in His Sixties Commits Fraud 139

Under the Pretext of Hiring Workers for the Golf Course

Thirteen Victims, Including He Leming, High Age, First Offense, Police Lawyer Hopes for Lenient Sentence

Yu Jintao (also known as Fusheng), a local man from this county, is sixty-two years old. He used to be in the business of jade and antiques, but recently became unemployed and destitute. He came up with an idea and, starting from the 12th of this month, went to the Xian Shi Amusement Park every evening, claiming that the Hongqiao Golf Course was planning to hire an additional fifty workers and staff because it was the summer vacation. He claimed to have a close relationship with the manager of the golf course, Fan Huichun, and that if anyone wanted to apply for a position, he could guarantee success. At that time, thirteen people, including He Leming, Zhang Dazhang, Cao Zhen, Zhang Baoyu, Zhang Shiding, Wang Acai, Gu Laisai, Zhou Amao, Shi Changfu, Xie Yushan, Xie Juqing, Wang Zhiying, and Xu Ronghai, all asked Yu to introduce them. Yu then demanded a corresponding reward. Except for He Leming and Zhang Dazhang, who each paid ten yuan, the rest each paid five yuan and six jiao. Starting on the 16th, Yu disappeared from the Xian Shi Amusement Park. The victims then realized that they had been deceived and searched everywhere for Yu's whereabouts. Finally, at 8:50 AM yesterday, they found Yu at the Sihai Inn, Room 2, on Tianjin Road. He Leming reported to the Old Gate Police Station, which ordered Chinese detective Lang Jintang and detective Lu Rongting to arrest Yu and bring him to the police station. Fake round chop books and other items were seized. When questioned about the whereabouts of the money he had swindled, Yu claimed that he had swindled money from another person in the Chinese Concession in West Shanghai, and after being discovered, he negotiated with the victim. He then invited the victim to a tea house at No. 12 Jiaozhou Road, Roberts Road in West Shanghai, and returned the money. Unexpectedly, several gangsters sitting at the next table overheard the matter and extorted all of his 138 yuan. Therefore, he claimed that he had no money left. He confessed that the whole thing was a scam and that the Hongqiao Golf Course had no intention of hiring anyone. The detectives then joined forces with the police detectives from the Public Security Bureau to arrest the three gangsters, Zhang Yifu and Hou, and the women Xu Lushi and Tang Chenshi, who had extorted Yu's money. They were temporarily detained at the Public Security Bureau. Yesterday morning, the police station handed Yu Jintao over to the First Criminal Division of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang explained the above situation and charged Yu with habitual fraud under Article 340 of the Criminal Code. He also stated that the defendant was old and had no prior convictions, and therefore hoped that the court would take these two points into consideration when sentencing. Cao Zhen and Xie Juqing then testified about their experiences of being scammed. When questioned, Yu Jintao admitted that he had resorted to this scam due to poverty and asked for leniency. After Magistrate Feng Shide reviewed the confession, he ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and postponed the sentencing.

Male and Female University Students' Affair Exposed, Leading to Lawsuit 142

A Love Story Between Two Intellectuals

The Defendant Has Consistently Failed to Appear in Court, Leading to an Order for Strict Summons

Lai Jiansheng, a 26-year-old Cantonese student in his fourth year at Datong University, met Liu Quanxian, a 17-year-old female student at Daxia University, at a dance hall last year. Both students were intellectuals, and they fell in love at first sight, embarking on a romantic relationship. Unexpectedly, due to their close affection, Liu became pregnant. As her abdomen grew larger, it became difficult to conceal, especially in the hot weather. Liu's mother, Madam Liu Xu, noticed this, questioned her daughter, and found Lai's photos and other items. After Liu confessed everything, she entrusted a student at Zhizhi College to write a letter to Lai, hoping for a resolution. At that time, if Lai had remained consistent, they might have become a couple. However, Lai avoided meeting them. Madam Liu and her daughter were angered by Lai's ungratefulness and resorted to the actions of rogue children, hiring a lawyer to sue in the District Court. The prosecutor filed a public prosecution. Yesterday, Judge Li opened the court session. Because Lai had never appeared in court, the plaintiff requested an arrest warrant for Lai, stating that he was about to graduate. The judge approved the request for a strict summons.

A Rescue Vehicle Overturned West of Luyang Bridge on Xihu Road Last Night 144

Two Dead, Two Injured, Driver Responsible for the Accident Detained

Xin Sheng News Agency reports that around 6:30 PM on the 17th, a rescue vehicle from the Xihu Long-Distance Bus Company was dispatched to Jiading to repair passenger car No. 51. The driver, Wang Dabao, drove to the west end of Luyang Bridge. Car No. 51 had already been repaired. The rescue vehicle immediately drove back. Unexpectedly, on the return trip, the driver, Wang Dabao, suddenly allowed Wu Xisheng, a tire repairman, to drive. Wu Xisheng's driving skills were not refined, and he was talking and laughing with his companions, thus becoming negligent. Near Bridge No. 168, the car body swayed, and he suddenly panicked. The front of the car swung erratically, causing it to overturn. The driver, Wang Dabao, and the attendant, Yu Desen, died on the spot. The injured trainees, Qian Xilian from Taicang, 20 years old, and the cook, Lin Songquan from Liuhe, were sent to the Zhenru Southeast Hospital by the traffic police stationed at the Luyang Bridge station. They have now been transferred to Dou Long Hospital, and their conditions are critical. The company prohibits employees from tampering with vehicles. Upon receiving the news, the company immediately dispatched personnel to the scene of the accident to investigate and sent the tire repairman Wu Xisheng, who caused the accident, to the Nanxiang Public Security Bureau for custody. They also requested the Jiading County Government for an examination, and it is reported that the families of the deceased have arrived at the scene to collect the bodies, and the company will provide compensation.

Nearly Septuagenarian Still Dares to Break the Law, Pan Xianting Accused of Fraud Under a False Name 146

Yesterday's Preliminary Hearing

Defendant Released on 1,000 Yuan Bail

Pan Xianting, a 68-year-old Suzhou native residing at No. 22 Yonghua Lane, Fangbanqiao Milu Road, in the French Concession, was reported to the French Concession Police by Chen Zhongqing (34-year-old Wuxi native) Gu Bingsheng (29-year-old Yangzhou native) Wang Guangyi Xu Wanrong (39-year-old Yangzhou natives) and others, residing at No. 2 Jiuan Lane, Jiaotong Road, Zhabei. They claimed that in February of the 24th year of the Republic, Pan claimed to be the general manager of the Jiande Iron Mine and, through the introduction of Yu Wenbin and Gu Zhongliang, entered into contracts to transport pig iron and serve as a foreman to recruit workers. They were defrauded of security deposits (including 867 yuan in security deposit under Chen Zhongqing's name, over 500 yuan for food supply, 190 yuan in security deposit under Gu Bingsheng's name, 680 yuan under Wang Guangyi's name, and 220 yuan under Xu Wanrong's name). After a long time, there was no news of actual operations, and Pan disappeared. Now they have finally found his whereabouts and requested the police to arrest and investigate. The policeman approved the request and sent Detective Li Deshu to arrest Pan and take him into custody. Yesterday, he was escorted to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special Court, where Judge Qiu Huan Ying interrogated him. Lawyer Fei Xizhen from the Police Department stated the case, briefly saying that the defendant was arrested for fraud. The Police Department still needs to investigate and requested a seven-day extension to investigate and then file a lawsuit for interrogation. Subsequently, the plaintiffs recounted the circumstances of the fraud one by one. When questioned, Pan Xianting denied the fraud and hired a lawyer to defend him. Because the defendant was old and sick, he requested bail. After verifying the confession, the court ordered a rescheduling for the 24th for further interrogation. The defendant was granted bail of 1,000 yuan with a guarantor who would ensure his appearance upon summons. Without a guarantor, he would be detained.

A Dance and an Instant Connection: Dancer Wishes to Grow Old with Dance Partner 147

To Gain Trust, Tong Rongsong Promised to Give the Woman 10,000 Yuan, Bank Employee Discovered a 1 Yuan Passbook Altered to 2,000. The Woman Accused the Man of Indecency and Forgery

Tu Xiaoying, a girl from Ningbo, is currently 18 years old and was raised by the Zhu family. Therefore, when Xiaoying worked as a dancer at the Victory Dance Hall on Beijing Road last year, she used the name Zhu Meizhen to accompany dances. Meizhen was young and beautiful, with a graceful figure and skilled dancing, so she was favored by many dance partners. In January of last year, Tong Rongsong, a Jiangdu native residing at No. 9 Jinle Lane, Weihaiwei Road, only 19 years old, went to the Victory Dance Hall to dance with several friends. Having long heard of Meizhen's reputation, he danced with Meizhen once and felt an instant connection. Afterwards, every time Tong Rongsong went to the Victory, he would have Meizhen sit at the table and accompany him, and his love deepened day by day, eventually leading to a relationship. They would secretly meet at inns. They even discussed spending their lives together. Therefore, Tong not only gave 3,000 yuan as a fee for Meizhen to sever ties with the Zhu family but also promised to give 10,000 yuan to gain her trust, first paying 2,000 yuan into a passbook at the China Industrial Bank, with the remaining 8,000 yuan to be paid later. Unexpectedly, when Meizhen took the passbook to the China Industrial Bank to withdraw money, the bank teller discovered that the passbook had been altered from one yuan to two thousand yuan and confiscated the passbook, contacting Tong Rongsong, but to no avail. Meizhen, believing that Tong's actions violated Article 227 of the Criminal Law regarding indecency and Article 201 of the same law regarding forgery, had her uncle, Tu Jianren, and her mother, Tu Chen, hire lawyer Peng Qixiu to file a lawsuit against Tong in the court, requesting punishment according to the above two articles and also attaching a civil lawsuit requesting damages and consolation money of 10,000 yuan each. Furthermore, because the defendant had a new love and was to marry another woman on the 17th of this month, they requested a swift arrest and investigation. This case has already been heard once, but because the defendant did not arrive, the hearing was postponed. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Tan Xinzhen continued the hearing in the Eighth Criminal Court. The defendant, Tong Rongsong, arrived with his defense lawyers Tang Huaiqun and Yuan Xilian. Tu Xiaoying (i.e., Zhu Meizhen) recounted the previous events, stating that in May, she had committed adultery with the defendant at the Yangzi Hotel, and the defendant promised to give her 10,000 yuan, first paying 2,000 yuan, etc. When she took the passbook to the China Industrial Bank to withdraw money, she discovered that it had been forged from one yuan to two thousand yuan, etc. When questioned, the defendant Tong Rongsong confessed that he had met Zhu Meizhen at the Victory Dance Hall in January of last year. After meeting, he would go to dance and ask her to sit at the table. At 2 AM on the night of May 6th, Zhu Meizhen finished dancing and returned home, and he accompanied her. Because the door was not opened, Zhu suggested that she would like to have a long night conversation with him, so they opened a room at the Oriental Hotel. That night, they did have a relationship, but there was no discussion of marriage. The passbook containing 300 yuan was given to Zhu as a gift in January of last year. In May of this year, he suddenly received a call saying that a Miss Tu wanted him to go. He went to Tu's house and was surrounded by seven or eight people who forced him to issue a 2,000 yuan IOU. At that time, someone produced a passbook and forced him to change the amount to 2,000 yuan. Then they drove him out, etc. Judge Tan verified the confession and ordered the case to be rescheduled for the afternoon of the 27th for further interrogation. The defendant was ordered to provide a guarantor for 5,000 yuan. Before the guarantee was submitted, he was allowed to be bailed out under the responsibility of his defense lawyer.

Rescued Hostage Dai Haiyi, Large Number of Kidnappers Apprehended in Xichang 148

Wuguidun Dingshu Town Xiaoxi Nei, Eight Previously Wanted Criminals Arrested, Where Did the Other Five Boys Come From?

On the morning of the 27th of last month, at around 7 AM, the kidnapping of five-year-old Dai Haiyi occurred at the home of Dai Keheng, a sand and gravel businessman at No. 20 Huaiyuan Lane, Hengfeng Road, Zhabei. For over a month, there has been no news. The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau ordered the Xinzha Branch to solve the case. After Detective Squad Leader Bao Ziying of Xinzha spent money to investigate, he learned that the hostage was hidden in Wuxi. The day before, he took his squad members to Wuxi by car and stayed overnight. On the afternoon of the 17th, he joined forces with Zhong Jihe, the leader of the Wuxi Public Security Bureau's Detective Team, Deputy Detectives Wang Bingsheng and Dai Shouquan, and several detectives to intercept a bandit boat outside Yinglong Bridge in Ximen, arresting bandits Chen Yi, a boatman, and Chen Youfang, two brothers. They then went to the thatched sheds in Qishuyan Wuguidun and other places, where they captured another bandit, Sun Xiaolong. They immediately interrogated him and learned that the hostage was hidden in Changzhou. At around 4 AM, Squad Leader Bao and others took a speedboat to their destination and discovered a small boat. They immediately arrested bandits Xia Shiwei, Guo Ruyang, and Xu Dapeng, three people. They further confessed that the remaining gang members were in Xiaoxi Nei, Dingshu Town. They immediately rushed there and saw a small boat moored in a small river. Inside the cabin, they found the hostage Dai Haiyi and five other boys, as well as a male and female bandit guarding the hostage. They were all taken to the Wuxi Public Security Bureau for detention overnight and were sent to Shanghai this morning.

The Sausage Casing Industry in Shanghai (Continued) 161

— Chief Editor of China Credit

(Twenty-eighth in the series "An Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce")

Current Status of the Sausage Casing Industry in Shanghai: The sausage casing industry in Shanghai is divided into three categories: (1) fresh sausage casing shops, which are small in scale and have relatively stable business; (2) sausage casing factories, which are subject to frequent changes, with the existing ones being supported by foreign merchants; (3) export companies, which are dominated by foreign merchants. The current status of each is described below:

Fresh Sausage Casings: The fresh sausage casing shops in Shanghai have an industry association, located in Nanlin Lane, Zhabei. There are twenty-odd members in the association, with capital ranging from 1,000 to 2,000 yuan, with the highest being no more than 9,000 yuan. Each morning, the shops receive anywhere from a little as thirty or forty pig sets to as many as one hundred pig sets. The number of pigs slaughtered daily in Shanghai is limited, so the operations of fresh sausage casing shops are actually quite small. A list of the fresh sausage casing shops is as follows:

Sausage Casing Factories: There are more than ten sausage casing factories in Shanghai, divided into Chinese and foreign-owned. However, the Chinese-owned sausage casing factories are all related to foreign merchants. It is recently reported that 45% of all sausage casing factories are directly or indirectly operated by German merchants. The business of sausage casing factories is mainly wholesale, which involves greater risks. 13% of Graduates from Colleges and Above are Unemployed 162

(Central News Agency, Nanjing, 18th) The Ministry of Education previously ordered all public and private colleges and universities to investigate the number of unemployed graduates from the 22nd and 23rd academic years in order to determine specific relief plans. Shanghai Education Bureau Orders the Closure of Dongfang Junior High School 163

The private Dongfang Junior High School on Tianbao Lane, Hai Lu, in this city, has been in turmoil since last year. The principals have been frequently replaced, the school is empty and desolate like a ruined temple, and there is no financial solution. The students are of complex backgrounds, and their thoughts and actions are often excessive. After repeated investigations by the Municipal Education Bureau, it was deemed that the school's foundations were shaky, its facilities were inadequate, and there was no hope for improvement. Fearing that it would mislead young people, the school has been ordered to close.

Small Number of Students at Waseda University in Japan Reject Supervisor Chen 164

One or Two Students Incite the Majority, Who Remain Unmoved

The Disturbance Subsides After School Warning (Tokyo Dispatch) Chen Cipu, our country's supervisor of students studying in Japan, returned to China on the 4th of last month to report on his work, following an order from the Ministry of Education. Shortly after Chen's return to China, a small number of students at Waseda University suddenly launched a campaign to reject Chen. Regarding this matter, the Tokyo Jiji Shinpo on May 15th and the Shanghai Times on the same day both carried detailed reports from the Dentsu News Agency. The situation at that time was quite tense, but since then, there has been no significant development. After extensive inquiries by reporters, it was learned that the matter has been settled. The course of events and the truth are briefly recorded as follows:

Since Chen Cipu was dispatched to Japan last August, he has adopted strict supervisory methods to rectify the affairs of students studying in Japan, which inevitably dissatisfied one or two students. After Chen returned to China on the 4th of last month, a student named Li from Waseda University proposed rejecting Chen at a meeting of the Chinese Students Association of the school. There were originally hundreds of Chinese students at the school, but only fifty or sixty people attended the meeting that day. Li's reasons for proposing the rejection of Chen were that Chen was "bureaucratic" and used "high-handed tactics," which were quite empty. Although many of those present did not agree, they did not openly oppose it. As a result of the discussion, Li and Weng were temporarily elected as executive committee members to contact student groups in other schools, but the students in other schools were unmoved. After learning of this matter, the Waseda University authorities warned Li not to create trouble, summoned Li and others for a talk, and strictly ordered them to focus on their studies and not to cause disturbances again, otherwise they would be expelled to maintain school discipline. Since Li and others did not receive support from students in other schools and were subjected to this warning, they stopped their activities, and the disturbance subsided invisibly. Reporters further learned that Li, who proposed rejecting Chen, and Weng, who was elected as an executive committee member, had both been reprimanded by Chen for certain incidents and harbored resentment in their hearts. This attack on Chen was purely a means of venting personal anger as a form of revenge.

The Place of Origin of New Higher Education Students in the 24th Academic Year 169

The Number of Students from the Northeast Has Decreased by Nine-Tenths Compared to Before

The Ministry of Education recently compiled statistics on the places of origin of new students admitted to colleges and universities nationwide in the 24th academic year. Among them, there were a total of 426 students from the four northeastern provinces (Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe). According to the Ministry of Education's statistics when the four northeastern provinces had not yet fallen, there were a total of 4,281 students from the Northeast studying in schools at that time (Liao 3003, Ji 865, Hei 327, Re 84). Compared before and after, there are now only one-tenth as many, a decrease of nine-tenths compared to before. Looking back on the past and present, how can one not feel emotional? The place of origin of new students admitted to colleges and universities nationwide in the 24th academic year is recorded below:

Jiangsu 1689, Zhejiang 937, Anhui 511, Jiangxi 323, Fujian 563, Guangdong 1593, Guangxi 284, Hunan 703, Hubei 433, Sichuan 556, Guizhou 51, Yunnan 49, Liaoning 312, Jilin 88, Heilongjiang 14, Hebei 1176, Henan 532, Shandong 525, Shanxi 441, Shaanxi 89, Gansu 15, Ningxia 1, Suiyuan 20, Chahar 17, Rehe 12, Qinghai 1, Xinjiang 21, Mongolia 1. An Evaluation of Yang Xiu's Achievements 182

— Huaiqing

Yang Xiu has stirred up a heat wave in our country's women's swimming world, and it is only natural that the people love and support her. However, the evil society uses distorted poses to achieve certain goals and fulfill certain wishes, which is hardly a blessing for the sports world.

Now Ms. Yang will represent China at the World Games. Her domestic achievements in this declining era should be considered quite satisfactory. But what hope does Ms. Yang have of participating in the World Games with her achievements? If we compare her achievements with the women's swimming achievements of previous World Games, we can know that Ms. Yang's hope, like that of other athletes, is generally hopeless, and the most hopeless.

The heat of society's love for Ms. Yang can be said to have reached above the boiling point. How will the young Ms. Yang use her eyes to distinguish the people unfolding before her, and how will she use her rationality to cope with the evil and distorted society, especially as a school-age girl, a female athlete with a promising future? She must not be misled, and her athletic skills are likely to stop there.

At the National Games in Nanjing and Shanghai, and the Far Eastern Games held in the Philippines, Ms. Yang's victories are indeed worthy of enthusiastic praise from society. However, the fact that Japanese women did not participate in the 10th Far Eastern Games was also a major reason for Ms. Yang to enjoy such extraordinary honor. Although we do not fully understand the level of Japanese women's swimming, to sum it up in one sentence, Ms. Yang's achievements are still far behind them, and even further behind the world swimming level. We should actively encourage Ms. Yang and kindly urge Ms. Yang to reach a truly bright state, and to shed a ray of dawn on the Chinese women's sports world.

Guangdong Swimming Team Mixed Swimming Competition 188

Since the Guangdong Swimming Team of this city started practicing at the city swimming pool some days ago, all the team members have enthusiastically participated. Mixed Swimming: In addition to actively promoting swimming training, the team has decided to hold a funfair for the team members once a week, in order to connect feelings and increase interest. Mr. Li has decided to hold a mixed swimming competition this Sunday. First, the team members who attend that day will be divided into several teams. Half of each team can swim and half cannot. Those who can swim are in the shallow water. Each team that can swim and cannot swim occupies one bank. At the sound of a command, the first swimmer from each team swims to the opposite bank and drags back the one who cannot swim. Then the third person continues. Each time, only one person is allowed until all the non-swimmers of that team are dragged back. The team that finishes in the shortest time wins.

Business News Financial Gold Bidding Buying Interest Still Very Strong

—Result: Increased by Two Yuan—

The gold market was stable yesterday because of continued strong buying. Although it turned weak midway, it turned stable again in the end because of positive news from the government bond market. Early in the morning, the overseas silver market showed that British and American silver shrank by half, and the Montreal forward silver price did not change uniformly. Exchange rates shrank. London raw gold fell by two pence. The central bank's listing was announced, and both British and American silver were flat. Customs gold fell by two fen. The standard gold price listing was reduced to 1124 yuan and 3 jiao. Pre-market trading outside the market opened at 35 yuan. Huixiang, Dingkang, Fuxingyong, etc., all advanced, gradually rising to around 41 yuan. The morning opened high. After opening, the market turned from stable to declining due to strong selling and slight selling by the bulls, falling below 40 yuan. Buyers took advantage of the low prices to trade. The HSBC bank listing was announced, and both British and American silver were flat, gradually pulling up, with a slight rebound. The silver balance tax listing shrank by half a fen, and soon returned to flat. After entering the market, the supply and demand were not smooth, resulting in a mediocre market situation. At noon, it hovered around 40 yuan. The market was still flat later, and then rose due to the positive news from the government bond and commodity markets boosting buying interest. However, there were still many who took profits at the high prices, and the market gradually flattened after the high prices. The market conditions for today will be recorded later.

Seafood: New Ningbo Kelp Production Poor 204

New Ningbo kelp has seen increasingly active arrivals from various mountains in recent days. Over the past two days, a total of 657 bags, weighing over 800 dan, have been transported. As a result, high-quality, clean white kelp is particularly scarce. Merchants are reluctant to buy because of the poor quality. Fortunately, new arrivals were allocated according to the numbers to begin with. However, prices have already softened from twenty-three yuan to twenty-one yuan and five jiao, a sharp drop of three yuan compared to the previous session. Because the new kelp production is of low and inferior quality, various merchant guilds continue to purchase aged stocks. Street inventories are gradually decreasing, and dealers are unwilling to sell quickly. Currently, the market price for high-grade kelp is thirty yuan, with common kelp at twenty-eight yuan. The market is firm, and there is no sign of softening for the time being. Aged northern kelp stocks have long been depleted, and new arrivals are scarce.
