Shen Bao Literary Supplement

Homecoming 212

—Yao Mu

It has been almost ten years since I returned to the city of × where I grew up. The kind old relatives I cherished in my childhood, the old family estate and garden where I once lived for many years, the community lanterns in the Lantern Festival, the welcoming gods parade that shook the entire city—especially the naive minds—even though they brought a bit of melancholy, they occasionally flashed in my memory, but only flashed. A person forever wandering in the world is not easily touched by the homesickness.

Several days before Qingming, my old father, who has added new white hairs, especially called me before him and solemnly said:

"The ancestral graves have not been swept and worshiped for several years. Your ancestors are truly disheartened. They haven't even had a bite of cold pork."

"Um"—seeing that I didn't respond to him much, he indignantly continued, "In the future, I will never trouble you when I die. Water burial would be cleaner! I raised four sons..." He then routinely complained and vented his usual grievances about his sons to me.

I also routinely listened from beginning to end, without a word of change, until he poured out the small ivory tiles from the box and began to play his ivory tile divination, then I answered lightly:

"Let's go this Saturday, to avoid the crowds during Qingming." Having been confined at home for half a year, I was really tired and just wanted to change places. Returning to my hometown was naturally not a matter of objection.

In these few years, even the village ferry has changed glaringly. Although the hull is still a flat-bottomed building ship with red and green patterns in the style of the Middle Ages, the dark and narrow cabin is always crowded with people, steaming with a unique fishy smell, but at least the "dining hall" has inserted some modern devices in a nondescript way: in front of the flower niche enshrining the sea god, there are no rows of canvas horses, but two rows of "roast pig plate" style bunk beds with soft mattresses; the kerosene lamp has been replaced by a bright electric light, the leisurely tea bowl has been replaced by a practical thermos bottle, and even the natural toilet has been replaced by a flush toilet—the main symbol of modern civilization.

However, the chaos and noise before the ship still dominate: the ferryman is holding a flickering lantern and shouting loudly to attract passengers, the porters are carrying luggage, and under the fiery sky dyed by the neon lights on both sides, this corner of the world constitutes a very lively oil painting. In the ferry, vendors are shouting and interweaving, passengers are fighting for berths, and a loud and turbid local accent that sounds like a quarrel is a bit unfamiliar. The drum has struck, and the ship is about to leave. The chaotic heat wave subsided a little. On the rattan chairs in front of the dining room, several diners were chatting leisurely:

"Old He, you've gained a lot of weight. No wonder Old Jin said you've stored more than one acre of grain this year," a middle-aged man with a badge said with a smile.

"Don't listen to his nonsense!" The answer came from a country gentleman-like person, "He's the one who got rich."

"Didn't the grain price rise from three yuan to more than six yuan in these two months?" another person interjected.

"But I bought three thousand bags when it was five yuan. Who dares to do more business with legal tender? The profit is limited. Who is like Old Jin, whose warehouse is packed full?" Old He's face revealed a look of annoyance.

"In this depressed year, you old folks should be content. I heard that the fan and grocery stores are all crying bitterly!"

The old man didn't answer, got up and walked outside, the corners of his flattened mouth hung with a smug smile, and his bald head with a few sparse hairs floating with brilliance.

After the boat guard casually checked the luggage, the ship really set sail. The fiery red light and the noisy voices gradually faded away, leaving only the gurgling of water and the occasional whistle that sent the tired passengers to sleep one after another.

After changing to a long-distance bus, I arrived at the city of ×, which was exactly the time of the morning market. A huge swarm of flies was beginning to manage their day's life. On the road, on the backs of pedestrians, and on the faces of children, these small black animals were gathered. The fish stalls on the roadside, the salted fish hanging in front of people's eaves, and the rice shops' rice baskets were all densely covered with black spots, like black sesame seeds. With every step, the fly formation in front of me buzzed and scattered, flying up and pouncing on my face, drilling into my ears and nostrils. Being in this kingdom of flies, I realized that this was my true hometown.

The newly built roads lay idle, with only a few rickshaws, miscellaneous old stalls, and food stalls being the actual users of the roads. The stone-paved streets and alleys were still occupied by sugarcane residue, dog feces, human feces, and sewage. There are indeed many Western-style buildings rebuilt from old houses, but all the old-fashioned things like "dwarf legs" are preserved. Some houses still have the long-backed bamboo chairs that the grandmothers sat on. The community altars piled with stones on the streets and alleys are still full of strips of paper with the names of adopted sons and daughters, but the ancestral halls are even more desolate than before: the flagpole is broken, the flagpole stone has collapsed, and the sides of the gate are overgrown. We have no ancestral hall, no ancestral house, and even the closest relatives are scattered, so we had to settle down in a step-aunt's house. Some distant cousins were already there waiting for us.

"Uncle, blessings, cousins are really capable..."

"If grandma were alive, I don't know how happy she would be!"

"It's nothing, it looks good outside!" My father answered coldly, not knowing if he was a little proud or touched a sore spot. I said "ashamed" to myself.

The old women stroked my eldest child, asking about his height and weight, and said to me with a smile, "You were just as big as this when your grandfather had his birthday!"

Yes, also at the age of this child, I often came here with my mother. At that time, my grandfather, uncle, and cousins were still alive, and it was the heyday of my uncle's family. The three-section house had just been newly built, and in the courtyard full of wisteria in front of the hall, there was a large goldfish tank with artificial mountains, which was the most attractive thing to me. Then came marrying cousins, marrying cousins, and visiting relatives was like running water, very lively. But since my grandfather died, my uncle's family began to decline! In a few years, more than half of the family members died, the house was haunted by ghosts during the day, and later sold two-thirds of it. Even the eldest cousin, who was more than fifty years old, had to make a final struggle and return to South America. Now the step-aunt lives only on the bookstore side, the goldfish tank has long been gone, and even the uncle's beloved orchids have all died.

"How is old He of Hejiatang?" My father was talking to a distant great-uncle who had followed him in the past, reminiscing about the old family situation in × city.

"No need to mention them. Taibaofu and Dongyuanzhuang have all fallen apart. Hejiatang, alas, people call it Little Macau. The children either blow or gamble. It is said that there are eighty or ninety guns!"

"Opium pipes, right?" "I don't know, no defeat is strange!" "The old man hides in the countryside, eating steamed food, eating up the family property, how can that last long!" My father once again expressed his old claim that heroes should start a career outside.

Before the offerings were prepared, I took the time to visit Li Ma, who had served me since childhood. The low wall made of snail shells was a bit crooked, and as soon as I entered the gatehouse, I saw that the pine tree in the courtyard was still as green and lush as before, but in a few years, Li Ma was a bit old. The jade hairpin that still held her hair bun had a lot of white hair, and her toothless mouth was even more crooked.

"Aming!" She opened her mouth and called my nickname, "When did you come back?" Seeing my child beside me, she pulled him to her side and asked, "This is your old man, right? How many younger siblings do you have? Alas, how cute! He looks just like you when you were little. Fourth brother, I didn't expect Li Ma to have the life to see your child."

"Call her grandma," I said to the child. "My darling," she said, while reaching into her clothes, and after a long time, she took out two copper coins and stuffed them into the child's hand, "A little something, buy something to eat."

"Are you doing well? Are you still sewing palm fans?" I saw that her house was still piled with some scattered palm fans and a water tank soaked with rattan threads.

"Isn't it still the same!" She sighed slightly, "Sewing palm fans is not always available, my eyes are almost failing, I can only sew ten a day, earning two cents each."

I looked at her carefully, and her eyes were indeed a little dim. The scene of her and my grandmother sewing fans quickly under the glass lamp in front of the gods at dusk suddenly appeared before me.

After she asked a little about my family situation, I bid her farewell.

"I don't even have a cup of tea to give you, this house is too dirty," she said politely to us, "Are you living at your aunt's house? I'll come see you later."

"We're just about to ask you to help us divide the pork among the relatives!"

Out of the suburbs, the grave mountains were already visible in a row. I don't know how many times I've followed my father and brothers to the graves, but I always can't recognize the way. In the past, the roadside was densely piled with green sunflower fields, some of which were abandoned, and some were drooping with withered yellow leaves. However, the azaleas on the tops of the mountains and beside the pits were always as red as blood. The mountain road was very flat, but walking in the dry and hot sunlight like early summer was a bit tiring. The children, sweating all over their heads, still jumped and bounced along, while my father leisurely took healthy steps, talking and laughing with his great-uncle, and sometimes stopped to point out whose grave mountain it was.

The roast pig was barely prepared, but it was still simple: at least the exaggerated tomb couplets like "Good Fortune in the Resting Place of the Ox" and "Fine City Standing Tall" were not prepared. My father respectfully worshiped at a grave and always lingered for a while. The stereotyped geomancy theory flowed out of the mouth of my father, who was confident in his knowledge of surveying.

"This is the toad spitting fire," my father said, pointing and painting as if reciting his proud article, "Look, the back is resting on the Five Old Peaks, and the front is facing Guifeng as a case, and the case means a pen holder. In the past, it would at least send out a county magistrate!"

"The water in front is a little bit leaked, it doesn't gather wealth," the great-uncle also pretended to be an expert and criticized.

"But, distant water is good, it doesn't matter," my father quickly defended. "In the past, my great-uncle turned against his in-laws for the sake of fighting for this mountain, and even now some people want to intrude."

Then they talked about the geography of the surrounding graves and the family history of the gentry of × city. Which mountain sent out a few licentiates, and which mountain sent out tens of thousands of family property, they talked with great interest.

The children were either picking wildflowers by the graves or staring at the sugarcane on the walls, shouting that they were thirsty.

I remember when I was eight or nine years old, I would jump up happily when I heard that I was going to sweep the graves. When I visited the graves of my uncle's family, I often followed, because I wanted to pick azaleas in the mountains, dig up branches of water, and beat the iron statues of Qin Hui and his wife with sugarcane tails in front of the Yue Fei Temple in Beijiao (the custom of Chongyang). The big meal in front of the grave was even more likely to arouse my greed. When the adults were sipping and tasting, I also ate sugarcane and gnawed on pork bones, especially the flavor of roasted goose liver, which still makes people nostalgic. Now, the tomb sweeping that looks like a formality, this kind of joy can only be found in memory!

When entering the city, the sun was scattering dew, and our return route happened to pass through Hengchong, where I was born, and the old things of my childhood suddenly welled up in my heart. The snow-white stone road and stone bridge under the moonlight, the fire and the continuous figures of people and lights in the water when the bride passed by, everything seemed poetic.

"Your father was born here," my father said to his child with a smile, pointing at the Situ Ancestral Hall.

"Huh! This broken house!" With the child's words, I could no longer deny the desolate scene here.

The narrow Situ Ancestral Hall was tightly closed, the walls were covered with moss, the small ditch in front had dried up and was piled with garbage, and the small stone bridge crossing the ditch was also broken. The ancestral halls on both sides were quiet, a bit like the scene after a war. The beautiful picture revolving in dreams and ideals is ultimately different from the reality before my eyes!

Search 213

—He Ruirao

At the end of the autumn sky, a thin horse rides through the desolate wilderness in the cold evening light. The withered bushes cover countless barren graves; in the barren graves, lie buried thousands of eternally unawakened dreams. On the short stump slanting into a pile of earthen hills, there still remains a vague inscription: ——The upper officer Zhang Deqiang is buried here. In the west wind, the desolate smoke is vast, where can one find the memories of billowing smoke? Does the setting sun also understand human affairs? Silently writing out the infinite sadness of all ages! The rider disappeared in the vast twilight; yet from the hazy distance, came a mournful neigh of a horse!

Grassland Night 214

— Lin Na

With the last train of the twelve-thirty shift gone, this small train station built in the mountains and fields returned to silence. In the sky, a round full moon faintly hung, illuminating the wide countryside until it appeared bright white, suddenly looking like a world coated in mercury.

At this time, flagman Wang Da was yawning as he stepped out of his shack and headed towards the small path made of pebbles that led to the village. He was a young, quiet, and honest farmer. Two years ago, after his aunt's husband, Rong Qian, who lived in the big city, became the deputy stationmaster of Baishui Station, he was introduced to this remote place to work as a flagman. At that time, he was still a loner, very content with his job. Eating, working, sleeping... all followed the routines of a docile person, and his days passed as peacefully as a stream. But soon, someone threw a boulder into his peaceful stream, causing it to ripple and become unsettled. That was when he met a young widow named Ma in the village. This young widow was short, only twenty-five or twenty-six years old, with a pair of small star-like eyes and a serene and sincere smile. Although she often wore mended and tattered clothes, they were always clean. Her loud voice, her sincere smile, and her polite manner often had a great allure to young farmers, but the villagers were somewhat afraid of her and disdained to pay her any attention.

When the stationmaster held his thirty-fifth birthday celebration at his newly built mansion in the village, Wang Da became aware of her beauty, which shocked him. He realized for the first time that he was captivated by a woman. After the last train of the twelve-thirty shift left, he often walked back and forth outside her window, softly whistling love songs in the local dialect. She opened her window and echoed him in a dreamy voice, and he boldly climbed in through the window. That's how they fell in love.

Wang Da knew a lot about her. She had no family, no land, just a widow who had lost her husband, a mother who had lost her daughter, a lonely village woman who had been insulted and harmed. She had a boisterous and almost mad personality, a common trait among frustrated young women in this remote area, drinking and casually sleeping with any farmer she liked. Sometimes she would get drunk in the fields and run along the ridges, singing lewd songs, while young farmers chased after her with willow branches, singing along in coarse voices. Sometimes she would be pinned to the ground, her clothes torn off, her hair disheveled, forced to dance by several men playing the sanxian. She was treated as a toy to be casually entertained, she was humiliated and harmed; yet, she got her work and necessary food from it.

Wang Da hated her wild and unrestrained lifestyle; however, he couldn't live without her. His life was lonely and barren, and he was deeply infatuated with her beauty. "I must try to advise her, I should say to her like this: Masha, this kind of life is terrible, you have the good qualities of a respectable woman, you must strive to be a respected and welcomed woman!..." Thinking of this, he smiled. He believed that just a word from him would have a profound effect. However, he was immediately overshadowed by another thought and felt cold. He saw her drunken, shameless laughter, he saw her lewd dancing, he remembered the lyrics from her filthy mouth, he remembered the mournful sound of the sanxian and the foolish faces of the musicians, burning with excitement. He was furious. "This is such a terrible, terrible life!..."

By this time, he had stepped through the first gate of the village. In the distance, the stationmaster's family lived in a Western-style house, the only civilized building in this remote place. The large glass windows still reflected a strong ray of light. The village had become even more silent and desolate. He walked slowly, unconsciously stopping for a while in front of the stationmaster's house, then turned around the corner of a mill and headed towards the widow Ma's thatched house.

The door was fastened with a hemp rope, which he noticed after knocking for a while without hearing a response from inside. "Where has this hussy gone again?" he said angrily to himself, and was about to turn around and go back to the workshop. But something seemed to be bewitching him, making him feel reluctant and hesitant. "No! I can't go back, no matter what, I must find her," he muttered to himself. Suddenly, he cocked his head and listened, because he heard a burst of laughter, a bold, shameless clamor, wafting over from the silvery edge of the grassland.

He felt angry, but also a little sad, he was stung by jealousy. So he hurried off towards the grassland.

On the grassland, the laughter and shouts of a group of people were resonating. The sanxian accompanied shameless songs. He heard a sharp voice, it was the voice of the widow Ma! It was also trembling there, causing his chest to burn with anger.

He stood for a while, thinking, then hid under a juniper tree, squinting and looking out over the grassland. He saw two lively little stars twinkling in the naked grassland, under the misty sunlight. It must be her, he believed. He also saw the two little stars suddenly start running, followed by a young, rude shadow. They were running along the grassland, along the ridges, running... Finally, the little stars lost their light and fell to the ground, which meant that her disheveled hair or any part of her body was grabbed and pinned to the ground. Then he heard a sharp, hoarse struggle, screaming, with lewd curses, but the sound of the sanxian and the shameless songs quickly drowned everything out. Wang Da trembled, he regretted coming here, he hated this beautiful moonlit night, he was angry at this group of shameless thugs: why do people want to humiliate her?…

He thought angrily.

On the grassland, fatigue was spreading among these young men and women. They walked back to the village, excited and satisfied, singing as they went. But she, the widow Ma, was still there, she might be longing for something, or perhaps expecting something, but no one could tell, because she was pondering while facing the moon. The grassland was quiet, and everything had become more desolate due to the moon's embrace. Wang Da, realizing that everyone had run far away, quietly crawled out from under the juniper tree and quickly walked towards the grassland.

He ran, ran, ran recklessly, finally stopping behind her. This sudden appearance made her feel flustered and shocked, but he just smiled coldly and sat down beside her silently. A terrible storm was raging in his heart and causing him great pain.

Suddenly, in the silence, he was startled by a sharp, hoarse laugh. He looked up, and it was that pair of little stars twinkling with light, it was that lewd laughter from those filthy, shameless lips. He remembered: the singing, the mournful sound of the sanxian, the naked dancing, he was furious, his hands were trembling. An impulse, an unconscious excitement was urging and tormenting him. So, he unnaturally reached out his hand, pulled out the waist knife he was carrying from his pocket for self-defense, and angrily thrust it into her back. Crimson blood spurted out like a gushing spring. She only laughed weakly twice, then limply collapsed into his warm embrace.

Turmoil 215

— Li Sanlang

His painfully myopic eyes stared at the blank manuscript paper in the dark night, feeling the cold air seeping from the cement floor, which made him feel numb and achy as he wrote. His wife occasionally raised her troubled eyes, stealthily watching his motionless back bent over the desk, holding her breath, only hearing the rustling sound of the pen tip moving across the paper. The short hand on the table clock was already past twelve. She sighed wearily:

"Wei! Go to sleep, your eyes are important! Don't go blind!"

He turned his head and glanced at her disheveled hair and her sallow face, reminding him of her beautiful, plump face when they were newly married four or five years ago, now sucked dry and pale by demons. Her charming eyes had been replaced by red, swollen circles. What about himself? He was still wearing the same plain glasses from four years ago, and every night he continued to work with painful eyes. For his family, for his children, for the mounting debts, for the food of the family of six, for the four months of rent, he had to forget his own suffering, which felt like being cruelly whipped, and write those worthless articles, squeezing out bitter juice.

He sighed, glared at the ticking clock, and crept into the warm quilt during the quiet moments when the north wind was blowing outside the window.

In the morning, he was awakened by the clamor and the crying of the children. He hurriedly put on his clothes and ran out of the door of the small room in the attic. He saw his elderly mother moving her toothless mouth, her sunken small eyes tightly wrinkled, her high cheekbones sharply protruding, her face looking even more yellow and frightening. He, as her son, had grown accustomed to this sight and didn't find it particularly scary. She grumbled and scolded, waving her hands and stamping her feet as if she was acting in a play. He couldn't help but feel annoyed. He blinked his eyes and glanced down at his wife, whose tear-stained face was pouting with grievance, and the baby in her arms was crying incessantly.

"What's wrong? Why are you making such a racket first thing in the morning!"

"She scolded me for no reason and even wanted to hit me." Tears streamed down his wife's face.

"You young people, I'm like an old nanny to you! But you have no conscience, I have no clothes to wear, you have money, but you won't give me a penny!"

"What's worth you making such a fuss? If you don't want to do it, let her do it. I told you not to do it a long time ago, but you insisted on doing it, making a racket all day long!"

His wife was sobbing, and the child was crying loudly.

"She even dropped the child, you heartless woman!"

"I never thought you would treat me like this one day, you have money but you won't do me a favor, you won't even pay off my debts."

"God knows, my forty-odd dollars of manuscript fees this month, thirty dollars for rent, ten dollars for you to pay off debts, but you spent it all on pointless favors. And you still pressure me..."

He almost burst into tears, anger and sorrow intermingling:

"The older you get, the more heartless you become!"

But his mother threw something on the ground with a thud and started stomping her feet like a madwoman, shaking her head, walking back and forth, stretching out her wrinkled hands, pointing to the sky and the earth, and sighing deeply:

"It's all the women who encouraged you..."

This heartbreaking scene made him forget that the reason for their increasingly eccentric personalities and their inability to get along was due to the difficult social environment. Because of their various provocations, his heart was filled with a mixture of sorrow and resentment:

"If you keep arguing like this, I can't take it anymore, I'm leaving!"

He thought he was speaking from a sincere resolution, rubbed his tired and painful eyes, looked at his mother's mad appearance, sighed, and lowered his head.

"Then leave, I don't want such an unfilial son either."

This time, the flames of long-suppressed distress in his heart truly erupted.

"I'm leaving, don't regret it, don't..." He had always been reluctant to leave this prison-like home, retreating from the path of progress back into this declining circle, just trying to find a way to keep them from starving. Now, that fantasy had disappeared like a dream, and a string of memories made his eyes water.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Essays

Seeking a Jail Meal to Fill the Stomach 216

— Jia Wei

It seems that someone once said that people live their lives in contradictions. Judging from the facts, this is absolutely true. Not to mention that a person's thoughts and thoughts, thoughts and actions are constantly in contradiction and conflict; even the progress of history and society does not develop forward in contradiction. As for today's chaotic socio-economic organization, contradictory situations are exposed everywhere. For example, "Give me liberty, or give me death" is a rational motto for human survival. Our ancestors, our companions, fought and sacrificed heroically for "freedom" in order to achieve collective and individual survival—freely. However, today, we have many, many people, some of whom are forced, enslaved, and deprived of "freedom," while others "voluntarily" (?) sell their freedom and sacrifice their freedom in order to obtain temporary survival.

For example, recently, a fact has proven this to us: According to reports, the First Special District captured a thief named Chen Jinhai, who is over thirty years old; he was sentenced to three years in prison by the First Special District Court for theft. Last September, he was released from prison and went to Nanjing, where he committed another crime and was sentenced to six months; this February, he came to Shanghai and sneaked into the Gongwu Stage and the Great World three times to steal. He was recently arrested and sent to the First Criminal Division of the Special Court. When the judge questioned him, Chen Jinhai admitted to the repeated theft crimes without hesitation. He even asked the court to punish him severely, saying, "I can't find a way to make a living outside. After being sentenced, I can still have jail meals to fill my stomach." Sure enough, in addition to the judge sentencing him to two years in prison, he even felt that the sentence was too short.

Imprisonment, as everyone knows, is a punishment for criminals who are temporarily or permanently deprived of "freedom." Not to mention that daily life there is many times lower than that of ordinary people, but being confined day and night without the slightest freedom is not what people want! Many criminals who are in prison demand that the court give them a light sentence and reduce their sentence, hoping to encounter an "amnesty" and get out of prison early to "restore my freedom." These are all reasonable and normal things. But now, some people voluntarily ask to be severely punished and imprisoned for a long time. This seems to be contrary to reason. However, the reason is that "after being sentenced, there are still jail meals to fill the stomach."

Originally, "appetite" is not only a function that we humans, from adults to newborn infants, cannot lack, but also a prerequisite for survival shared by general animals. However, "eating is difficult" has become a common saying among people today. For the sake of "eating," humans compete with each other, exclude each other, and even commit crimes, commit suicide, and kill each other... This has become an inevitable trend of the times! Therefore, even though everyone knows that imprisonment deprives them of freedom, there is still something that "fills the stomach" and prolongs their survival function.

Here, we really don't know how many people in today's social organization are like Chen Jinhai? Moreover, we don't know how many people have noticed this kind of social contradictory fact and are trying to thoroughly change it?

Suosuo Beach (Part 1) 217

— You Qi

Following the usual practice, I took the leftover coarse rice from last night, which was hanging under the eaves of the house, added some lukewarm water, and swallowed it. It was quite difficult to find some pickles in these mountains and fields, no, even some very plain soy sauce was often lacking.

The shopkeeper catered to small merchants passing by, and occasionally some simple travelers. There was no need to prepare a large amount of supplies in terms of demand. One trip to the market could cope with three or five days. In Lao Nao's imagination, there would be no danger of running out of supplies. However, this time, our group made him dizzy. He wanted to scrounge up some soy sauce, but the result was still a disappointment.

—Never mind, the rice has already gone into the stomach, who cares if there are vegetables or not—A Huang glanced at Lao Zhang, Lao Zhang understood this tacit signal very clearly. He ran to the front and whispered a few words to the two porters, raised his purple-brown arm, and shouted in a voice that the porters didn't want to hear—

—Let's go, head to Suosuo Beach!

So, we rushed out of Zhengzhi Street and headed onto the official road that was buried in the invisible path.

Standing at the head of Suosuo Beach, we began to consider, —travel by land or wade through the water? These two questions lingered in my mind, and no consensus was reached. Finally, it was decided to separate into two groups. Those who preferred to travel by land were free to do so, and those who wanted to wade were welcome to come. I joined the latter group, and jumped onto the large wooden boat that was next to the beach.

The porters' faces had a different expression, and the reason was not difficult to guess. From here to Xiejiachuan, the waterway was twenty li long. Although it was not a long distance (in the porters' vocabulary), life was tightly pressing down on them, not allowing them to breathe easily. It was extremely difficult to get a good night's sleep or enough to eat. If they could get twenty li of rest, they would probably consider it the ultimate luxury?

After that, a group of people led a portion of the luggage, and walked through the dense bushes. I couldn't see them, how could I describe them? Those porters' faces shared a common, indescribable expression!

The wooden boat did not have any equipment like awnings. It was very similar to the boats used to transport goods on the Suzhou River. There were two people rowing, one was an old man covered in frost, and the other was a child with a milky complexion. The capacity inside was quite large, with a sedan chair, four stretchers, five or six carrying poles, and a dozen or so passengers. The weight was also considerable.

Not far from where the boat was tied up, a large stone stood in the middle of the river. Many words were carved on one side, the largest two characters were "Divine Stone," and below were some stories about the Divine Stone. Asking the old man rowing the boat, he felt that it possessed "divine" energy. During stormy nights, when the hot summer weather was struck by sudden hailstorms, and the entire universe seemed about to explode, the "Divine Stone" would descend from the sky, graze the roofs of many villages and towns that were not built firmly, without being damaged at all. The stone roared, and stopped on the shore of the beach, allowing passing travelers to look at its majestic posture. The Divine Stone had considerable value.

In the Great Pine Forest 218

— Shen Jiaqian

Tales of the Jianghu

One summer, I wandered to a small city in the north, where I suddenly contracted a dangerous local epidemic. Looking back at the situation, it felt like a nightmare. The name of the epidemic was a palindrome, quite difficult to remember; even the name of that small city, I cannot clearly recall now. I only remember that more than ten li away from the small city was a great pine forest, and the story happened in that forest, a painful story that I will never forget!

The small city was surrounded by mountains, and in the summer, the dangerous epidemic spread everywhere. The owner of the inn where I stayed had once been a member of the Green Forest (bandits). When I fell ill, he personally concocted local herbal remedies for me, and it was not until the autumn coolness arrived that I escaped danger. For almost half a year, I did not pay him a single coin for lodging and meals, and he generously saved my life. When I wanted to continue my wandering life, he earnestly urged me to stay. He said:

"In the first half of my life, I killed and set fires, doing many wicked things. Now I run this inn to help travelers and make up for my sins. You are young and do not know the dark side of the Jianghu. It's not worth it to throw away your life for nothing. I simply want to keep you here to be my helper, but if you really want to leave, I won't force you."

I agreed without hesitation to stay at the inn. Originally, I was wandering everywhere with my life in the hands of others. I couldn't betray the owner's kindness, and perhaps living in that small city could increase my experience, because all kinds of Jianghu figures came and went in the inn every day.

The days passed quickly, and soon it was winter, with heavy snow falling. The inn had no business in the winter because the great pine forest was obscured by snow more than a foot thick, and the roads were impassable. Moreover, the great pine forest was not a clean place; passersby were often beheaded and hung upside down on the pine branches. But since the opening of that inn, those acts of robbery and murder had gradually decreased. After living in the inn for a long time, the owner knew my story. His name was Little Yellow Dragon, and his name was well-known in the northern regions. He was like a chivalrous thief in old novels, robbing the rich to help the poor. He had more than two hundred apprentices under him, all living with him. When he washed his hands (retired from banditry), his apprentices strongly opposed it. They were used to that kind of robbing life, and no one was willing to accept Little Yellow Dragon's distributed money and, as he instructed, start small businesses to make a living.

One day, while it was snowing heavily, we were drinking by the brazier. He threw the old Mauser pistol he wore at his waist onto the table and pointed at it, saying:

"It was this gun that I used to kill my favorite apprentice! He was the one who most opposed my washing my hands!"

The raging flames reflected on his purplish-red cheeks. His eyes stared at me without blinking, and he cried out with two drops of clear tears: "He looked exactly like you, child! That's why I want you to stay here. Seeing you is like seeing him."

It was the first time I had seen a rough man cry like a girl, and I was deeply moved by him.

"Now," he continued, "those two hundred-plus men have split into many small gangs and are still working as bandits, but they don't dare come near my place. But I know that one day I will be hurt by them. They hate me to the bone."

As the snow was about to melt, a merchant came to the inn. He stayed for two days, always talking to Little Yellow Dragon every day. He said that he wanted to go to the provincial capital to see his father who was ill, and he was carrying a lot of silver with him. He didn't dare to cross that great pine forest alone, but he didn't state his final request. Little Yellow Dragon patted his chest:

"I understand what you mean. I have a child watching the store. I'll help you with the trip!"

The next day they set off. Before leaving, Little Yellow Dragon drank a large amount of wine, loaded his old Mauser pistol with bullets, and told me to take good care of the store. He would send the merchant across the great pine forest and return immediately, at most in two days.

But on the fourth day, he still hadn't returned to the store. I remembered what he had said that night when he cried. Perhaps he had encountered some danger. Two more days passed, and he still hadn't appeared. I couldn't bear it any longer and went after him to the great pine forest. Because it was already the season of melting snow, the road was very muddy and difficult to walk, and I didn't know the way. For two days and nights, I got lost in the great pine forest, never able to get out of the forest's range. I hadn't eaten a grain of rice for two days, and I was so weak that I couldn't walk. I grabbed a small branch to support myself and walked in circles. When I fell to the ground, I found some clothes of both of them, hanging high on a large pine tree like torn banners, and a pair of dried persimmon bags were right beside me. After eating my fill, I ran wildly in the pine forest again, but I never found their bodies.

This is almost ten years ago, but when I write it down, it feels like it happened yesterday.

Radio Program Broadcast Script

Suzhou People (22) 219

— By Gu Wenzong

Liya (Snatching to speak): You're really something! You find it strange and laughable, don't you?

Jinghong: Oh! Please don't be upset. Look, your face is red, and your neck is getting thicker. I'm truly sorry! Miss Jin, please forgive me! (Followed by a contemptuous fake laugh.)

Liya (Coldly): Hmph! You don't need to apologize to me, and you don't need to deliberately stimulate me with that humorous laughter, friend! Oh! Suzhou sister! Goodbye.

Jinghong: Very well! My Suzhou sister, you should rest and recuperate. Pay attention to your health; that is the most important thing in life. Anger is most harmful to your health, Suzhou sister, go and rest, goodbye! Let's shake hands, even when angry, it doesn't mean one shouldn't be polite!

Liya: But politeness doesn't necessarily mean it won't give an angry person a headache.

Jinghong: Since you don't want to shake hands with me, I don't necessarily have to keep my hand out. Look, haven't I picked up my teacup to drink tea again? (Sound of drinking tea) Why don't you have a sip of tea before you go back?

News from the Theater Scene

Weekly Experimental Theater Revitalizes; Ant Troupe Performs at Lake Society

The Weekly Experimental Theater, after performing "The Proposal," "Freedom," and "Medicine" at the New Light Theater last week, has received much praise from all walks of life. However, the New Light's facilities are not suitable for public plays. Therefore, they have been contacting theaters more suitable for public play performances, but none have been successful due to conditions. Now they are doing their best to improve the shortcomings of the New Light as much as possible and have decided to perform next Sunday (the 21st). The plays are: "A Corner of the Metropolis" (Original by Xu Peiwai, published in the December issue of "Literature" last year), "Autumn Sun" (Author Zhang Geng, published in "Reading Life"), and "Smuggling" (Author Hong Shen, published in the recently released "Guangming Semi-Monthly").

At the same time, we received news that the Ant Troupe will also perform "Smuggling," "Who Killed the Baby," and "Horn, Third Script" at the Lake Society on Beijing Road on the 23rd (Tuesday).

Movie News

Grand Light Screens "A Message to Garcia" 223

Starring Huarez Pyle

Huarez Pyle, although born with a very ugly face, is praised by movie fans all over the world as an amazing artist. His clumsy, explosive, and witty acting skills are unparalleled in Hollywood. This time, he was invited by the 20th Century Fox Company to work with the handsome John Bowers and the beautiful actress White Beilan Stanley in the historical war epic "A Message to Garcia," The story of the film is taken from the Cuban people in 1898, who, under the leadership of General Garcia, revolted against the Spanish government. The United States intervened, but because Garcia was known to be leading his troops in ambush in the forest and his location was unknown, President McKinley personally ordered Lieutenant Rowan to take a secret letter to Cuba, try to deliver it to Garcia, and inform the landing site of the US military, so that they could unite and defeat the Spanish army. The performances of the three artists in this film have achieved great success. After watching this film, one feels that the historical facts of that year, which determined the fate of the three countries with a roar, are vividly brought to life. The film is released in Grand Light today (Sunday).

"Diamond King" to be Released Tomorrow at Jincheng Grand Theater 224

The long-awaited new film "Diamond King" starring famous actors has now been decided to be released at the Jincheng Grand Theater tomorrow (the 20th). This is news worth reporting to audiences who love domestic films.

The film is directed by Mr. Xu Xinfu. In the recent past, Director Xu's "Rogue Horse" must have left a deep impression on everyone's minds. This "Diamond King" is his more elaborate masterpiece. The tension and bizarre plot, and the grand and thrilling scenes are guaranteed. In terms of actors, Gu Lanjun plays a socialite, Wang Zhengxin plays the chief detective, Gu Meijun plays the female detective, and Xie Yunqing, Sun Yu, and Li Qing play the villains. Each performance is truly superb and seamless.

"Diamond King" tells you about the masks of civilized people in the upper class, the unscrupulous behavior of villains, the results of modernized women, and the indomitable spirit of law-abiding civil servants.

This is a work that hints at certain current questions! A rare opportunity, don't miss it.

"A Message to Garcia" Two Leading Actors White Beilan Stanley John Bowers

Grand Light Screens

"Shanghai" Premieres "New Soviet Youth" 225

The Shanghai Grand Theater on North Sichuan Road presents the amazing and latest Soviet film "New Soviet Youth," which the Soviet Union has devoted all its resources and a huge sum of money to actively develop film art and compete with Hollywood and the European film industry. It is a representative of the Soviet national people, and it uses very flexible methods to depict vividly the lives, entertainment, love, heartbreak, awakening, hard work, and inventions of modern Soviet youth, and how they finally achieve final victory. The whole film is full of youthful vigor, new atmosphere, and new life, and is a good example needed by all the peoples of the world, and also a good model needed by the modern Chinese masters of China who bear a major responsibility. It is indeed a truly and thoroughly cautionary film that instructs young people to have a spirit of perseverance, pulling back from the brink, and unremittingly struggling against adverse environments, and is a masterpiece that young people must see. The Chinese idiom "If you don't work hard when you're young, you'll only be sad when you're old!" is the purpose of the film, and at the same time, the world-famous "Soviet News" is also shown, including the grand celebration of the 18th anniversary of the Soviet revolution, which is very valuable.
